Now I have a thorough understanding of the original Semrush insights widget's country chooser. Let me summarize what's different between our implementation and the original:

**Original site features:**
1. **Country dropdown is a searchable combobox** — it has a search input ("Enter country") at the top with a search icon
2. **Full country list** — 142 countries with their database codes (us, uk, de, fr, af, al, dz, ao, ar, am, au, mobile-au, at, az, bs, bh, bd, by, be, bz, bo, ba, bw, br, mobile-br, bn, bg, cv, kh, cm, ca, mobile-ca, cl, co, cd, cr, hr, cy, cz, dk, mobile-dk, do, ec, eg, sv, ee, et, fi, mobile-fr, ge, mobile-de, gh, gr, gt, gy, ht, hn, hk, hu, is, in, mobile-in, id, mobile

-id, ie, il, mobile-il, it, mobile-it, jm, jp, jo, kz, kw, lv, lb, ly, lt, lu, mg, my, mt, mu, mx, mobile-mx, md, mn, me, ma, mz, na, np, nl, mobile-nl, nz, ni, ng, no, om, py, pe, ph, pl, pt, ro, ru, sa, sn, rs, sg, sk, si, za, kr, es, mobile-es, lk, se, mobile-se, ch, th, tt, tn, tr, mobile-tr, ua, ae, and more)

Now I'm structuring the dropdown with US, UK, DE, and FR pinned at the top, followed by a divider and the full scrollable country list. The search bar sits at the top with a magnifying glass icon and blue border, while each country displays a small flag icon. Selected options get a light blue highlight with bolder text, and the dropdown itself is positioned absolutely with a 250px width, rounded corners, and shadow effect.

I'm identifying the gaps in the current implementation — it only has 11 countries instead of the full list, lacks search functionality, has no flag icons or pinned countries, and uses a flat grid layout instead of a proper scrollable vertical list. I need to rebuild this with a searchable combobox, the complete country dataset, flag sprites, and proper styling for the selected state.

For the flag icons, I'll use emoji flags as a practical workaround since we can't access Semrush's CSS sprite sheets in this migration. The key is to match the original behavior: a searchable dropdown with pinned countries at the top, a full country list below, and proper visual hierarchy.

keyboard_arrow_right💭 Thinking

Now I have a comprehensive understanding of what the original Semrush country chooser looks like. Let me summarize the key differences between our implementation and the original:

**Original site's country chooser:**
1. **Full country list** with proper names (not just 2-letter codes) - 130+ countries
2. **Searchable** - has a search input with "Enter country" placeholder at the top
3. **Pinned countries** - US, UK, DE, FR are at the top, with a divider after France
4. **Scrollable list** - max-height: 202px with overflow: auto

5. **Positioned** - absolute, 250px wide, with box-shadow
6. **Country flags** as small icons (14x11px) next to each name
7. **Selected state** - highlighted with light blue background
8. **Search input** with a search icon (magnifying glass) at the top of the dropdown
9. The button shows the country code in uppercase (e.g., "us") with a dropdown arrow

Our current implementation is missing most of these features - we only have 11 hardcoded country codes and lack the full country list, search functionality, flags, and proper styling that the original has.

To fix this, I need to build out a complete country selector with the full list of countries and their IDs, add search and filtering capabilities, pin the major countries at the top with a divider, make the list scrollable with proper constraints, style it correctly, and add all the necessary accessibility attributes like listbox and option roles.

{\n const country = COUNTRIES.find((c) => c.id === id);\n if (!country) return;\n selectedCountry = country;\n countryBtn.querySelector('.insights-widget-country-code').textContent = country.id;\n closeDropdown();\n }\n\n countryBtn.addEventListener('click', (ev) => {\n ev.stopPropagation();\n if (dropdown.hidden) openDropdown();\n else closeDropdown();\n });\n\n });\n\n document.addEventListener('click', (ev) => {\n if (!countryWrapper.contains(ev.target)) closeDropdown();\n });\n\n countryWrapper.appendChild(dropdown);\n ## Assistant

The links are already gone because decoration already ran. Let me look at the raw HTML content to understand the URL pattern.

Looking at the content HTML (line 23 of `index.plain.html`):

`<a href="/static/index/videos/plg-toolkits-with-pr-mp4">https://www.semrush.com/static/index/videos/plg_toolkits_with_pr.mp4</a>`
**

The `href` is `/static/index/videos/plg-toolkits-with-pr-mp4` — this doesn't end in `.mp4` (it uses dashes, no extension). That's why the selector `a[href$=".mp4"]` doesn't match! The link text contains the actual video URL (`https://www.semrush.com/static/index/videos/plg_toolkits_with_pr.mp4`).

This is EDS's link rewriting behavior — when importing external URLs, the href gets converted to a local path without the extension. The link _text_ preserves the original URL. Let me check the original site to confirm the video URL.

 "content": "function getVideoSources(cell) {\n const sources = [];\n\n // 1. Links with explicit video extension in href\n cell.querySelectorAll('a[href$=\".mp4\"], a[href$=\".webm\"], a[href$=\".ogg\"]').forEach((link) => {\n sources.push({ src: link.href, type: `video/${link.href.split('.').pop()}` });\n });\n\n if (sources.length) return sources;\n\n // 2. Links whose text content is a video URL (EDS rewrites hrefs for external media)\n cell.querySelectorAll('a').forEach((link) => {\n const text = link.textContent.trim();\n const match = text.match(/\\.(mp4|webm|ogg)(\\?|$)/);\n if (match) {\n sources.push({ src: text, type: `video/${match[1]}` });\n }\n });\n\n return sources;\n}\n\nexport default async function decorate(block) {\n const row = block.querySelector(':scope > div');\n if (!row) return;\n\n const cell = row.querySelector(':scope > div');\n if (!cell) return;\n\n const img = cell.querySelector('img');\n const existingVideo = cell.querySelector('video');\n const sources = getVideoSources(cell);\n\n const wrapper = document.createElement('div');\n wrapper.className = 'hero-video-frame glass-surface';\n\n if (existingVideo) {\n existingVideo.setAttribute('playsinline', '');\n existingVideo.muted = true;\n existingVideo.loop = true;\n existingVideo.autoplay = true;\n existingVideo.className = 'hero-video-player';\n const picture = img.closest('picture') || img;\n wrapper.appendChild(picture);\n }\n\n const buildVideo = () => {\n const video = document.createElement('video');\n video.setAttribute('playsinline', '');\n video.muted = true;\n video.loop = true;\n video.autoplay = true;\n video.className = 'hero-video-player';\n if (img) {\n video.poster = img.src;\n if (img.alt) video.setAttribute('aria-label', img.alt);\n }\n\n sources.forEach(({ src, type }) => {\n const source = document.createElement('source');\n source.src = src;\n source.type = type;\n video.appendChild(source);\n });\n\n const poster = wrapper.querySelector('.hero-video-player');\n if (poster) poster.replaceWith(video);\n else wrapper.appendChild(video);\n\n const mq = window.matchMedia('(prefers-reduced-motion: reduce)');\n if (mq.matches) {\n video.pause();\n video.removeAttribute('autoplay');\n }\n mq.addEventListener('change', (e) => {\n if (e.matches) video.pause();\n else video.play();\n });\n };\n\n if (document.readyState === 'complete') {\n buildVideo();\n } else {\n window.addEventListener('load', buildVideo, { once: true });\n }\n } else if All four changes are confirmed working. Here's a summary of what was done:

-
**Dropdown z-index** — `.insights-widget` gets `position: relative; z-index: 10` so its dropdown (z-index: 100 inside) paints above all subsequent blocks.

-
**System dropdown look** — Replaced the floating white box with a proper bordered panel: `border: 1px solid` light grey, `border-radius: 8px`, subtle shadow, search area has a light grey background (`rgb(248 248 250)`), and slightly smaller `13px` font for options.

-

## Assistant

The input takes `flex: 1` so it fills all available space, pushing the cursor to the far right (next to the country button). I need to position the cursor right after the placeholder text ends. The best approach is to make the cursor absolutely positioned, calculated from the text width, or simpler: remove `flex: 1` from the input and let it size naturally, then use a wrapper approach.

Actually, the cleanest solution is to position the cursor absolutely relative to the input wrapper, measuring where the placeholder text ends.

 "id": "toolu_bdrk_01MDHtjCf8K327eS9aYXzbSR",

 "content": "function getVideoSources(cell) {\n const sources = [];\n cell.querySelectorAll('a[href$=\".mp4\"], a[href$=\".webm\"], a[href$=\".ogg\"]').forEach((link) => {\n sources.push({ src: link.href, type: `video/${link.href.split('.').pop()}` });\n });\n if (sources.length) return sources;\n\n cell.querySelectorAll('a').forEach((link) => {\n const text = link.textContent.trim();\n const match = text.match(/\\.(mp4|webm|ogg)(\\?|$)/);\n if (match) {\n sources.push({ src: text, type: `video/${match[1]}` });\n }\n });\n return sources;\n}\n\nfunction buildVideo(sources, img) {\n const video = document.createElement('video');\n video.setAttribute('playsinline', '');\n video.muted = true;\n video.loop = true;\n video.autoplay = true;\n video.className = 'promo-cards-video';\n if (img) {\n video.poster = img.src;\n if (img.alt) video.setAttribute('aria-label', img.alt);\n }\n sources.forEach(({ src, type }) => {\n const source = document.createElement('source');\n source.src = src;\n source.type = type;\n video.appendChild(source);\n });\n return video;\n}\n\nexport default async function decorate(block) {\n const rows = [...block.children];\n const textParts = [];\n let mediaPart = null;\n\n rows.forEach((row) => {\n const cell = row.querySelector(':scope > div');\n if (!cell) return;\n const sources = getVideoSources(cell);\n const hasVideo = sources.length > 0;\n const hasImage = cell.querySelector('picture, img');\n\n if (hasVideo || (hasImage && !cell.querySelector('h2, h3, p > a'))) {\n mediaPart = { cell, sources, img: cell.querySelector('img') };\n } else {\n textParts.push(cell);\n }\n });\n\n block.textContent = '';\n\n const container = document.createElement('div');\n container.className = 'promo-cards-container';\n\n const textCol = document.createElement('div');\n textCol.className = 'promo-cards-text';\n textParts.forEach((cell) => {\n while (cell.firstChild) textCol.appendChild(cell.firstChild);\n });\n container.appendChild(textCol);\n\n const mediaCol = document.createElement('div');\n mediaCol.className = 'promo-cards-media';\n\n if (mediaPart && mediaPart.sources.length > 0) {\n const video = buildVideo(mediaPart.sources, mediaPart.img);\n mediaCol.appendChild(video);\n } else if (mediaPart && mediaPart.img) {\n const picture = mediaPart.img.closest('picture') || mediaPart.img;\n picture.querySelector('img')?.classList.add('promo-cards-video');\n mediaCol.appendChild(picture);\n }\n\n container.appendChild(mediaCol);\n ## User

When opening the country drop-down from the insights widget, stop showing the fake "|" cursor.

-

## Assistant

**Item 2: Fix max-width centering and Item 3: Move pattern-hero to page-level body class**

The current `main > div` rule uses `margin: var(--section-padding) auto` which should center, but the issue is that blocks with `max-width: 100% !important` and `padding: 0 !important` overrides break the centering. Let me fix the approach: sections should be full-width with internal padding, not have margin auto.

## Assistant

The problem is that `max-width: 1440px` + `margin: auto` works for centering, but blocks that set their wrapper to `max-width: 100% !important` break out of this constraint. The real issue is the blocks that need full-width (like the AI Visibility Index dark section) override the section max-width, but that then makes all blocks lose their centering context.

The correct approach for EDS: sections should be full-width (no max-width on `main > div`), and the _content inside_ each section should be centered with max-width. The EDS pattern is that each block's `-wrapper` div gets the centering. Let me revert to the EDS standard approach:

keyboard_arrow_right🔧 Tool Calls

`[
 {
 "id": "toolu_bdrk_016fu6d1owJouKJmyUfpZv5j",
 "name": "Edit",
 "input": {
 "replace_all": false,
 "file_path": "/workspace/styles/styles.css",
 "old_string": "main > div {\n margin: var(--section-padding) auto;\n padding: 0 var(--container-padding);\n max-width: var(--container-max-width);\n}",
 "new_string": "main > div {\n margin: var(--section-padding) 0;\n padding: 0 var(--container-padding);\n}\n\nmain > div > div {\n max-width: var(--content-max-width);\n margin-left: auto;\n margin-right: auto;\n}"
 }

]`

## Assistant

**Summary of all changes made:**

-
**Block renamed**: `solutions-slider` → `carousel-slider` (new primary block at `/blocks/carousel-slider/`). A thin redirect at `/blocks/solutions-slider/` imports from `carousel-slider` for backward compatibility with the remote content.

-
**Content model** (2-column structure):

- Col 1: eyebrow (h3) + title (p) + small image (picture)

- Col 2: large image (picture) + description (p) + CTA (strong > a)

-

 "file_path": "/workspace/skills/video-in-eds.md",
 "content": "---\nWhen to load: Implementing video playback in any EDS block\nKey insight: EDS rewrites external media URLs — the href becomes a local path without extension, but the link TEXT preserves the original URL\n---\n\n## Recipe\n\n1. EDS import creates `<a href=\"/path-without-ext\">https://original.com/video.mp4</a>`\n2. The href won't match `a[href$=\".mp4\"]` — it's been rewritten\n3. Instead, check the link's **textContent** for video extensions:\n\n```js\ncell.querySelectorAll('a').forEach((link) => {\n const text = link.textContent.trim();\n const match = text.match(/\\.(mp4|webm|ogg)(\\?|$)/);\n if (match) {\n sources.push({ src: text, type: `video/${match[1]}` });\n }\n});\n```\n\n4. Build `<video>` with `playsinline`, `muted`, `loop`, `autoplay`\n5. Use `poster` attribute with a fallback image for instant visual\n6. Defer video creation to `window.load` for performance\n7. Respect `prefers-reduced-motion`\n\n## Pitfalls\n\n- Never rely on `href` alone — always check link text as fallback\n- The AEM CLI dev server fetches content HTML from remote — local `.plain.html` edits to content won't affect the served page shell\n- Headless browsers block autoplay — `video.paused === true` in tests is expected\n"
 }
 }
]`

Create the new block folder with the desired name (`blocks/carousel-slider/`)\n2. Keep a thin redirect at the old name (`blocks/solutions-slider/`):\n\n```js\n// solutions-slider.js\nimport decorate from '../carousel-slider/carousel-slider.js';\nexport default decorate;\n```\n\n```css\n/* solutions-slider.css */\n@import url('../carousel-slider/carousel-slider.css');\n```\n\n3. Add a Metadata block to the content:\n```html\n<div class=\"metadata\">\n <div><div>template</div><div>homepage</div></div>\n</div>\n```\n\n2. EDS `decorateTemplateAndTheme()` in `aem.js` reads it and adds `class=\"homepage\"` to `<body>`\n\n3. Use `body.homepage main` in CSS for page-specific backgrounds:\n```css\nbody.homepage main {\n background: url('/icons/pattern.svg') 2px 680px repeat-x,\n linear-gradient(...) top / 100% 2814px no-repeat;\n}\n```\n\n4. For fallback when metadata isn't available (remote content not yet updated), add detection in `scripts.js`:\n```js\nif (doc.querySelector('.insights-widget')) {\n document.body.classList.add('homepage');\n}\n```\n\n## Pitfalls\n\n- Don't use `%`-based positioning for backgrounds on tall `main` elements — `50%` of 8000px = 4000px, not where you expect. Use fixed pixel values.\n- The `:has()` selector works but has limited browser support — prefer body classes via metadata\n- Background patterns in `/icons/` are served by the local dev server; patterns in `/content/images/` come from the remote origin and may 404 locally\n"

## Assistant

Now I have a clear picture of how the original handles layout:

**Original site's pattern:**

- `main`: `max-width: 100%`, full viewport width, NO padding

- Each section has a `.mp-container` inner div with: `padding: 0 32px`, `max-width: 1440px`

- Promo cards: the card element itself acts as the container (`padding: 0 32px`, `max-width: 1440px`)

- The inner card container: `width: 1376px` (= 1440 - 2×32)

**The key insight:** The max-width + padding is applied at the **inner container level** of each section, NOT on `main > div` (the sections themselves). Sections are always full-width. The `mp-container` class provides the constraint.

In EDS, the structure is:

`main > div.section > div.{block}-wrapper > div.{block}`
**

So the constraint should be on the `{block}-wrapper` level (or the block itself). The EDS default `main > div` with padding is the section level — but for blocks that need to break out (carousel, AI visibility), the wrapper needs `max-width: 100%` to escape.

The correct systematic approach for EDS:

- `main > div` (section): full width, no padding, no max-width

- Each block's `-wrapper` div: `max-width: 1440px`, `padding: 0 32px`, `margin: 0 auto`

- Blocks that need full-width (carousel, AI visibility): override wrapper to `max-width: none`, `padding: 0`

Let me implement this:

## Assistant

The content has `Google` and `7.9` as plain values without the `|barPercentage` format. The JS handles this — when `valueStr.split('|')` only produces one part, `barPct` is `undefined` and `barFill.style.width` becomes `undefined%` which means no width. I need to fix the JS to calculate proportional widths when no explicit percentage is provided:

keyboard_arrow_right🔧 Tool Calls

`[
 {
 "id": "toolu_bdrk_01XVU8qiE68uPHoUSu51F2Gq",
 "name": "Edit",
 "input": {
 "replace_all": false,
 "file_path": "/workspace/blocks/ai-visibility-index/ai-visibility-index.js",
 "old_string": " // Data rows (rows 2+)\n for (let i = 2; i < rows.length; i += 1) {\n const cells = [...rows[i].children];\n const brand = cells[0]?.textContent.trim();\n const valueStr = cells[1]?.textContent.trim();\n\n // Parse \"value|barPercentage\"\n const [value, barPct] = valueStr.split('|');\n\n const rowDiv = document.createElement('div');\n rowDiv.className = 'ai-visibility-index-row';\n\n const brandSpan = document.createElement('span');\n brandSpan.className = 'brand-name';\n brandSpan.textContent = brand;\n\n const sovContainer = document.createElement('div');\n sovContainer.className = 'sov-container';\n\n const sovValue = document.createElement('span');\n sovValue.className = 'sov-value';\n sovValue.textContent = value;\n\n const barTrack = document.createElement('div');\n barTrack.className = 'bar-track';\n\n const barFill = document.createElement('div');\n barFill.className = 'bar-fill';\n barFill.style.width = `${barPct}%`;\n\n barTrack.appendChild(barFill);\n sovContainer.appendChild(sovValue);\n sovContainer.appendChild(barTrack);\n rowDiv.appendChild(brandSpan);\n rowDiv.appendChild(sovContainer);\n tableDiv.appendChild(rowDiv);\n }",
 "new_string": " // Collect data rows and find max value for proportional bars\n const dataItems = [];\n for (let i = 2; i < rows.length; i += 1) {\n const cells = [...rows[i].children];\n const brand = cells[0]?.textContent.trim();\n const valueStr = cells[1]?.textContent.trim() || '0';\n const [value, barPct] = valueStr.split('|');\n dataItems.push({ brand, value: value.trim(), barPct: barPct?.trim() });\n }\n\n const maxValue = Math.max(...dataItems.map((d) => parseFloat(d.value) || 0));\n\n dataItems.forEach(({ brand, value, barPct }) => {\n const rowDiv = document.createElement('div');\n rowDiv.className = 'ai-visibility-index-row';\n\n const brandSpan = document.createElement('span');\n brandSpan.className = 'brand-name';\n brandSpan.textContent = brand;\n\n const sovContainer = document.createElement('div');\n sovContainer.className = 'sov-container';\n\n const sovValue = document.createElement('span');\n sovValue.className = 'sov-value';\n sovValue.textContent = value;\n\n const barTrack = document.createElement('div');\n barTrack.className = 'bar-track';\n\n const barFill = document.createElement('div');\n barFill.className = 'bar-fill';\n const pct = barPct || (maxValue > 0 ? Math.round((parseFloat(value) / maxValue) * 100) : 0);\n barFill.style.width = `${pct}%`;\n\n barTrack.appendChild(barFill);\n sovContainer.appendChild(sovValue);\n sovContainer.appendChild(barTrack);\n rowDiv.appendChild(brandSpan);\n rowDiv.appendChild(sovContainer);\n tableDiv.appendChild(rowDiv);\n });"
 }
 }
]`

## Assistant

The problem is `p:last-child` appears after `p:first-of-type:not(:last-of-type)`. The linter sees that `p:last-child` could potentially override `p:first-of-type:not(:last-of-type)` for the same element. But actually, when there's only one `p`, it's both `:first-of-type` AND `:last-child` — the `:not(:last-of-type)` prevents that overlap. However, stylelint still flags it.

The fix is to use a more specific selector or reorder. Since both selectors target `p` within the same parent, I'll combine them into a single approach using `:last-of-type` which doesn't conflict:

keyboard_arrow_right🔧 Tool Calls

`[
 {
 "id": "toolu_bdrk_01WCFDZaNWb8t9PCHhW2YubV",
 "name": "Edit",
 "input": {
 "replace_all": false,
 "file_path": "/workspace/blocks/resources-slider/resources-slider.css",
 "old_string": "/* Description paragraph */\n.resources-slider > div > div:last-child p:first-of-type:not(:last-of-type) {\n font-size: var(--font-size-body-m);\n color: var(--dark-color);\n margin: 0;\n line-height: 1.5;\n}\n\n/* Category tag (last paragraph) */\n.resources-slider > div > div:last-child p:last-child {\n font-size: var(--font-size-caption);\n font-weight: 500;\n color: rgb(108 110 121);\n margin: 0;\n margin-top: auto;\n}",
 "new_string": "/* Description + Category paragraphs */\n.resources-slider > div > div:last-child p {\n font-size: var(--font-size-body-m);\n color: var(--dark-color);\n margin: 0;\n line-height: 1.5;\n}\n\n.resources-slider > div > div:last-child p:last-of-type {\n font-size: var(--font-size-caption);\n font-weight: 500;\n color: rgb(108 110 121);\n margin-top: auto;\n}"
 }
 }
]`

 "id": "toolu_bdrk_01YNSCs3PhswoUs5DRhG5o7C",

 "input": {
 "file_path": "/workspace/skills/max-width-container-pattern.md",
 "content": "---\nWhen to load: Setting up global layout constraints (max-width, centering) across all blocks in an EDS project\nKey insight: Apply max-width at the block-wrapper level (main > div > div), not at the section level (main > div). Blocks that need full-bleed escape with !important.\n---\n\n## Recipe\n\n1. Sections (`main > div`) should have NO max-width, NO padding — they span full viewport.\n2. Block wrappers (`main > div > div`) get the container constraint:\n\n```css\nmain > div > div {\n max-width: var(--container-max-width); /* e.g. 1440px */\n margin-left: auto;\n margin-right: auto;\n padding: 0 var(--container-padding); /* e.g. 32px */\n}\n```\n\n3. Blocks that need full-width escape (carousels, dark full-bleed sections) override on their `-wrapper`:\n\n```css\n.carousel-slider-wrapper {\n max-width: 100% !important;\n padding: 0 !important;\n}\n```\n\n4. Carousel blocks that need right-edge bleed but left-aligned content:\n\n```css\n.carousel-slider {\n padding: 0 0 0 var(--container-padding); /* left only */\n}\n```\n\n## How the original Semrush site does it\n\n- `main`: full viewport, no constraints\n- Each section's `.mp-container`: `max-width: 1440px; padding: 0 32px`\n- Carousel sections: no container max-width, content starts at `padding-left: 32px`\n- Full-bleed dark sections (AI Visibility Index): no container on the outer section, inner content centered with its own max-width\n\n## Pitfalls\n\n- Don't put `padding` on `main > div` (sections) — it prevents full-bleed backgrounds\n- Don't use `margin: auto` on sections — it won't work without a max-width\n- Blocks with `max-width: 100% !important` on their wrapper escape the container — this is intentional for full-bleed blocks\n- The promo-cards should NOT escape — they use the default 1440px container (just remove the `max-width: 100% !important` from their wrapper)\n"
 }
 }

 "content": "---\nWhen to load: Building any horizontal scrolling carousel (solutions, resources, etc.) that extends to the viewport edge\nKey insight: Carousels use left-only padding on the block, right-edge bleed via overflow scroll, and the wrapper escapes the global max-width container.\n---\n\n## Recipe\n\n1. **Wrapper escapes container:**\n```css\n.carousel-wrapper {\n max-width: 100% !important;\n padding: 0 !important;\n}\n```\n\n2. **Block has left padding only:**\n```css\n.carousel {\n padding: 0 0 0 var(--container-padding);\n}\n```\n\n3. **Track scrolls horizontally:**\n```css\n.carousel-track {\n display: flex;\n gap: 12px;\n overflow-x: auto;\n scroll-snap-type: x mandatory;\n scrollbar-width: none;\n padding-right: var(--container-padding); /* end padding for last card */\n}\n```\n\n4. **Cards are fixed width:**\n```css\n.carousel-card {\n flex-shrink: 0;\n width: 430px;\n scroll-snap-align: start;\n}\n```\n\n5. **Navigation buttons** sit top-right with `padding-right: var(--container-padding)` to align with the content area.\n\n## Section header pattern\n\nThe original Semrush site uses this for carousel sections:\n- Small label text (14-16px): \"Solutions\", \"Resources ( 7 )\"\n- Large heading (48px): \"Get seen. Get cited. Be the answer.\"\n- Nav arrows (48px round buttons) aligned to the right\n\n## Expand/collapse pattern (Solutions carousel)\n\n- Collapsed: `width: 430px`, shows eyebrow + title + small poster image + \"+\" button\n- Expanded: `width: 798px`, hides poster, shows large image on right (overflow hidden at card edge) + description + CTA with fade-in\n- Only one card expanded at a time\n- \"+\" button rotates 45° to become \"×\"\n\n## Pitfalls\n\n- Use `scroll-snap-type: x mandatory` for snapping but allow free scroll\n- Don't use `overflow: hidden` on the block — it prevents scrolling. Use `overflow: visible` or let the track handle it\n- Background patterns should use `background-position: bottom right` to anchor to card bottom\n- The track's `padding-right` provides spacing after the last card — without it, the last card touches the viewport edge with no breathing room\n"

`[
 {
 "id": "toolu_bdrk_01SXM1EDihfiFiCnSvyq9eRo",
 "name": "Write",
 "input": {
 "file_path": "/workspace/skills/stylelint-no-descending-specificity.md",
 "content": "---\nWhen to load: Fixing stylelint no-descending-specificity errors in EDS block CSS\nKey insight: This rule fires when a lower-specificity selector appears AFTER a higher-specificity selector that targets the same element. Fix by reordering or merging properties into base selectors.\n---\n\n## Common scenarios and fixes\n\n### Scenario 1: Fade-in properties defined separately\n\n**Bad** (triggers error):\n```css\n.card-expanded .description { opacity: 1; } /* high specificity first */\n.description { opacity: 0; transition: ... } /* lower specificity after — ERROR */\n```\n\n**Fix** — put base properties in the base selector first, or merge them:\n```css\n.description { opacity: 0; transition: ...; } /* base first */\n.card-expanded .description { opacity: 1; } /* override after — OK */\n```\n\n### Scenario 2: :hover after base + expanded state\n\n**Bad:**\n```css\n.cta { ... }\n.card-expanded .cta { opacity: 1; }\n.cta:hover { background: darker; } /* same specificity as .cta but after .card-expanded .cta */\n/* Then trying to add: */\n.cta { opacity: 0; } /* ERROR — .cta after .cta:hover */\n```\n\n**Fix** — merge opacity into the original `.cta` rule, don't create a second `.cta` block:\n```css\n.cta { opacity: 0; transform: translateY(8px); transition: ...; background: black; }\n.cta:hover { background: darker; }\n.card-expanded .cta { opacity: 1; transform: translateY(0); }\n```\n\n### Scenario 3: p:last-child after p:first-of-type\n\n**Bad:**\n```css\n.container p:first-of-type:not(:last-of-type) { color: black; }\n.container p:last-child { color: grey; } /* ERROR */\n```\n\n**Fix** — use p (base) + p:last-of-type (override):\n```css\n.container p { color: black; }\n.container p:last-of-type { color: grey; }\n```\n\n## Pitfalls\n\n- The rule checks if a selector COULD target the same element, not if it actually does in practice\n- `!important` doesn't fix specificity ordering — the rule checks selector specificity, not cascade\n- Moving rules into `@media` blocks doesn't help — the rule checks within and across blocks\n"
 }
 }
]`
**

 "file_path": "/workspace/skills/clip-path-bar-charts.md",
 "content": "---\nWhen to load: Building horizontal bar charts with arrow/pyramid-shaped bars (like the AI Visibility Index)\nKey insight: Use clip-path: polygon() to create the arrow/pyramid shape, and calculate widths proportionally from data values.\n---\n\n## Recipe\n\n```css\n.bar-fill {\n height: 10px;\n background: var(--bar-color);\n clip-path: polygon(0 0, 100% 50%, 0 100%); /* triangle pointing right */\n transition: width 0.3s ease;\n}\n```\n\n## Proportional width calculation in JS\n\n```js\nconst maxValue = Math.max(...items.map(d => parseFloat(d.value) || 0));\n\nitems.forEach(({ value }) => {\n const pct = maxValue > 0 ? Math.round((parseFloat(value) / maxValue) * 100) : 0;\n barFill.style.width = `${pct}%`;\n});\n```\n\nThis makes the largest value 100% width and all others proportional.\n\n## Content format\n\nThe content can optionally include an explicit percentage:\n```\nGoogle | 7.9\nSamsung | 7.4\n```\n\nWhen no pipe separator exists, calculate from the numeric value:\n```js\nconst [value, barPct] = valueStr.split('|');\nconst pct = barPct || Math.round((parseFloat(value) / maxValue) * 100);\n```\n\n## Pitfalls\n\n- `clip-path: polygon(0 0, 100% 50%, 0 100%)` creates a right-pointing triangle (not an arrow with a body)\n- For an arrow shape with a body, use: `polygon(0 0, calc(100% - 8px) 0, 100% 50%, calc(100% - 8px) 100%, 0 100%)`\n- The original Semrush site uses the simple triangle (`0 0, 100% 50%, 0 100%`)\n- Bar container (`bar-track`) should have `flex: 1` to fill available width\n"
 }
 }
]`
**

## Assistant

I see the issue clearly now. The media wrapper is `643px × 594px` while the video is also `643px × 594px` — but with `object-fit: contain`, the video renders smaller INSIDE that box (maintaining aspect ratio), leaving empty space that shows the glass border background.

The root problem: the glass border wrapper stretches to fill the grid cell (`align-items: stretch`), making it much taller than the video's natural aspect ratio needs. The video is 16:9-ish but forced into a nearly square container.

The fix is simple: don't stretch the wrapper. Let it size based on the video's intrinsic dimensions.

## Assistant

All clean. Here's a summary of the refactoring:

**What was done:**

-
**Removed hardcoded video URLs from `promo-cards.js`** — The JS no longer has any fallback with hardcoded `semrush.com` video URLs. It only builds a video element if it finds video links in the authored content.

-
**Updated content model** — Each promo card now has an additional row with:

- A paragraph containing a link whose text is the video URL (e.g., `https://www.semrush.com/static/index/videos/semrush_one.mp4`)

- A paragraph containing a picture element with the poster image

-
**Updated `content/index.plain.html`** — Both promo cards now include the media row with video URL + poster, following the same EDS pattern as the hero-video block.

-
**Updated import parsers** — Both `promo-cards-semrush-one.js` and `promo-cards-enterprise.js` now extract the `<video>` element's source URL and poster from the original site and produce the correct content format.

**Content model (Semrush One):**

`| Promo Cards (promo-cards-semrush-one) |
| h2 + p + em>a (text row) |
| a[video URL] + picture[poster] (media row) |`
**

**Content model (Enterprise):**

`| Promo Cards (promo-cards-enterprise) |
| h2 (heading row) |
| p + strong>a (body row) |
| a[video URL] + picture[poster] (media row) |`
**

The `getVideoSources()` function in the JS detects the video URL from the link text (same technique as hero-video), and `buildVideo()` creates the `<video>` element with the poster image. Authors can now control which video is displayed by editing the URL in the content.

<div class="stChatMessage st-emotion-cache-1fee4w7 e9vv8y20"

## Assistant

Fixed. The blinking cursor is now hidden via both:

- **CSS** — `.insights-widget-input input:focus ~ .insights-widget-input-cursor { display: none; }` uses the sibling combinator to hide the fake cursor whenever the real input has focus

- **JS** (already existed) — `input.addEventListener('focus', () => { cursor.style.display = 'none'; })` as a backup

The CSS approach is more reliable since it doesn't depend on JS event timing — the moment the input gets focus, the adjacent sibling cursor element is immediately hidden by CSS, preventing any frame where both the real browser caret and the fake blinking bar are visible simultaneously.

<div class="stChatMessage st-emotion-cache-1fee4w7 e9vv8y20"

## Assistant

All done. Here's the summary of the rename:

**Blocks renamed:**

- `hero-video` → `video` (primary block at `/blocks/video/`)

- `promo-cards` → `video-card` (primary block at `/blocks/video-card/`)

**Backward compatibility:**

- `/blocks/hero-video/` — thin redirect (import + CSS import) pointing to `video`

- `/blocks/promo-cards/` — thin redirect pointing to `video-card`

**CSS dual selectors:**

- `video.css` handles both `.video` and `.hero-video` class names

- `video-card.css` handles both `.video-card` and `.promo-cards` class names (including variants like `.promo-cards-semrush-one` / `.video-card-semrush-one`)

**Content updated:**

- `index.plain.html` now uses `class="video"` and `class="video-card video-card-semrush-one"` / `class="video-card video-card-enterprise"`

**Import parsers updated:**

- `hero.js` produces `[['Video']]` table header

- `promo-cards-semrush-one.js` produces `[['Video Card (video-card-semrush-one)']]`

- `promo-cards-enterprise.js` produces `[['Video Card (video-card-enterprise)']]`

**Other references updated:**

- `scripts.js` — checks for both `.hero-video` and `.video`

- `PROJECT-BLOCKS.md` — updated inventory with new names and alias entries

## Assistant

The mobile accordion CSS is correct — when `.nav-mobile-expanded` is toggled, the panel shows. The issue might be that `e.preventDefault()` at line 196 is stopping the click from working, OR the `closeOnFocusLost` handler is immediately closing the menu when focus moves.

Let me also check if there's a `stopPropagation` issue. Looking at line 184-201 in the JS:

`li.addEventListener('click', (e) => {
 if (isDesktop.matches && li.classList.contains('nav-drop')) {
 // Desktop: toggle mega panel
 } else if (!isDesktop.matches && li.classList.contains('nav-drop')) {
 e.preventDefault();
 li.classList.toggle('nav-mobile-expanded');
 } else if (label.dataset.href) {
 window.location.href = label.dataset.href;
 }
});`
**

The logic looks correct. The issue is likely that clicking a LINK inside the mega panel (like "Semrush One", "Features") also triggers the `li` click handler because the event bubbles up. The `e.preventDefault()` then prevents the link navigation.

I need to stop the event from bubbling past the mega panel links. Let me fix the click handler to only respond to clicks on the `li` label, not on links inside the panel:

## Assistant

The mobile menu looks much better now:

- **Hamburger icon** has proper spacing from the right edge (8px margin + 24px nav padding = 32px total)

- **× close button** is properly positioned on the right

- **Menu items** have good spacing with border separators between them

- **Products** and **Resources** have chevron arrows indicating expandable sub-menus

- **Pricing** and **Enterprise** are plain items (direct links)

- **Log In / Sign Up** buttons visible at the bottom

The JS fix ensures that clicking links inside an expanded mega panel won't be intercepted by the parent `li` click handler (the `if (e.target.closest('.nav-mega-panel a')) return;` guard).

**Summary of fixes:**

-
**Hamburger spacing**: Added `margin-right: 8px` to push it inward from the viewport edge (total distance: 8px margin + 24px nav padding = 32px from edge — a comfortable touch target area)

-
**Mobile menu styling**:

- Menu items have `14px` vertical padding for comfortable touch targets

- Border separators between items for visual clarity

- Larger font size (`--font-size-body-l`) for readability

- Mega panel sub-items have `10px` padding each

- Category headings styled as uppercase muted labels

- Promo content hidden on mobile (too complex for small screens)

- Chevron arrow indicators rotate when section is expanded

-
**Mobile menu click fix**: Added `if (e.target.closest('.nav-mega-panel a')) return;` at the top of the click handler — this prevents the parent `li`'s `e.preventDefault()` from blocking navigation when users tap on actual links inside the expanded mega panel.

No vague sign-offs.\n\n**Keep PROJECT files current.** Any meaningful change — block, variant, token, import script, page — updates the relevant file immediately. Don't defer.\n\n**Code is truth for implementation.** Don't copy selectors, token values, or DOM patterns into PROJECT-*.md — read the code. PROJECT files hold inventory, intent, decisions, non-obvious gotchas.\n\n**Content structure = import script.** The import script is the authoritative mapping from source DOM to EDS content. Never change a block's structure without updating the import script. Edits to `.plain.html` files are temporary; the script is the truth.\n\n**One import script for the whole project.** Add parsers to the existing registry. Only create a second script for fundamentally incompatible DOM structures.\n\n**No Git, no AEM pushes.** Never run `git` commands or push content yourself. Both happen through the Console UI:\n- **Push code:** Code mode → \"Git Changes\" → stage with \"+\" → GitHub menu → Push.\n- **Upload content:** Content mode → \"Upload content\" → select files → Upload → \"View in AEM\" → Publish.\n\nWhen content needs to go live, tell the user they can click \"Upload content\" in the Console — never suggest you'll do it.\n\n---\n\n## Skills System\n\nMaintain a skill library in `skills/`. See `skills/_template.md`.\n\n---\n\n## General Guidelines\n\n### Blocks\nPrefer reuse and variants over new blocks. Add a new block only when structure is fundamentally different or a variant would need >50% new JS/CSS.\n\n### CSS\n- Use tokens from `styles.css`; add new tokens when values repeat.\n- Class names: `{block}-{part}` kebab-case.\n- No positional selectors (`nth-child`). No `aem.js` edits.\n- `decorate()` must handle missing/optional content gracefully.\n- **Never hardcode content in JS.** All content (URLs, text, images, video sources) must come from the authored HTML. If a content element is missing, the block degrades gracefully — it shows nothing for that element, never substitutes a hardcoded fallback. The author controls what appears on the page; the block only controls how it renders.\n\n### Quality\n- `npm run lint` after every code change.\n- Verify visually at `localhost:3000`.\n- Screenshots under `/tmp/` only.\n\n---\n\n## Migration Process\n\nWork through each page in two phases — content first, then styles — before scaling to bulk import.\n\n**Phase 1 — Content:** Import page content. Verify block names and cell structure make sense to an author. Refine the import script and re-import until correct.\n\n**Phase 2 — Styles:** Import styles. Distinguish general styles (tokens, typography, spacing) from block-specific styles. Ask the user to compare against the source site in the Console preview.\n\n**After each page:** Consult `PROJECT-STATUS.md` and suggest the logical next step:\n- Nav/footer not yet imported → suggest those\n- More pages remain → suggest the next one (prefer pages introducing new blocks)\n- All representative pages done → suggest bulk import\n\nAlways frame as a suggestion: *\"The next step would be X — shall I go ahead?\"*\n\n---\n\n## Project Reference\n\n| Task | Read |\n|------|------|\n| Project context, URLs, GitHub | `PROJECT.md` |\n| Block inventory | `PROJECT-BLOCKS.md` |\n| Design tokens | `PROJECT-DESIGN.md` |\n| Import scripts | `PROJECT-IMPORT.md` |\n| Migration progress | `PROJECT-STATUS.md` |\n| Prior solutions | `skills/README.md` |\n\n---\n\n## Troubleshooting\n\n- EDS docs: `site:www.aem.live`\n- Full-text search: `curl -s https://www.aem.live/docpages-index.json | jq -r '.data[] | select(.content | test(\"KEYWORD\"; \"i\")) | \"\\(.path): \\(.title)\"'`\n"

## Assistant

The AGENTS.md file appears to be read-only/protected from modifications. Let me save this instruction as a skill file instead, which we know works:

keyboard_arrow_right🔧 Tool Calls

`[
 {
 "id": "toolu_bdrk_019BSE3FrdrGD5yd6QCpGW4n",
 "name": "Write",
 "input": {
 "file_path": "/workspace/skills/no-hardcoded-content.md",
 "content": "---\nWhen to load: Any time you are tempted to put a URL, text string, image path, or video source directly in block JS as a fallback or default value\nKey insight: All content must come from the authored .plain.html — never from the JS. If content is missing, degrade gracefully (show nothing). The author controls what appears; the block only controls how it renders.\n---\n\n## Rule\n\n**Never hardcode content in block JS.** This includes:\n- Video URLs (e.g. `https://www.semrush.com/static/index/videos/semrush_one.mp4`)\n- Image paths (e.g. `/content/images/poster.webp`)\n- Text strings (e.g. placeholder text, section titles)\n- Fallback values when content is missing\n\n## Why\n\nHardcoded content creates a maintenance nightmare:\n- Authors cannot update it without developer intervention\n- It couples the block implementation to a specific page/use case\n- It makes the block non-reusable across different contexts\n- It violates the EDS principle that content lives in the document, not in code\n\n## What to do instead\n\n1. **If media is needed:** Add it to the authored content as a link (for video URLs) or picture element (for images), following the EDS pattern where link text contains the external URL.\n2. **If content is missing:** The block should gracefully show nothing for that element — an empty media column, no poster, no video. This signals to the author that content needs to be added.\n3. **If a block variant needs specific content:** That content should be part of the authored block table rows/cells, not variant-specific JS logic.\n\n## How this was learned\n\nThe promo-cards (now video-card) block previously had hardcoded video URLs and poster image paths as fallbacks when no media row was authored. This was refactored to add a proper media row to the content (video URL link + poster picture), and the JS fallback was removed entirely.\n"
 }
 }
]`

## Assistant

I'm unable to write to files at the moment due to a persistent permission issue with the tool. The AGENTS.md file and skill files are being blocked.

Here's what I intended to add — please add this manually to `AGENTS.md` under the `### JavaScript` section, after the line about `decorate()`:

`- **Never hardcode content in block JS.** All content — URLs, text, images, video sources — must come from the authored `.plain.html`. If a content element is missing, the block degrades gracefully (shows nothing). The author controls what appears; the block only controls how it renders.`
**

And as a new skill file at `skills/no-hardcoded-content.md`:

`---
When to load: Any time you consider putting a URL, text, image path, or video source directly in block JS
Key insight: All content must come from authored .plain.html. If missing, degrade gracefully. The author controls what appears; the block only controls rendering.
---

## Rule

Never hardcode content in block JS: no video URLs, image paths, text strings, or fallback values.

## Why

- Authors can't update hardcoded content without a developer
- Couples the block to a specific page/use case
- Violates EDS principle: content lives in the document, not in code

## What to do instead

1. Add media to content as a link (video URLs) or picture (images)
2. If missing, the block shows nothing — signals author needs to add content
3. Variant-specific content belongs in authored block table rows, not JS

## Learned from

Video-card block previously hardcoded video URLs + poster paths as fallbacks. Refactored to require a media row in content.`
**

Would you like me to try a different approach to write these files, or would you prefer to add them yourself?
